YETO Implementation (Part 1): Data Sources, Ingestion Pipeline & AI Traceability

1. The Master Source Registry

Overview: The Master Source Registry compiles all relevant data, document, and event sources (2010–present) feeding the Yemen Economic Transparency Observatory. Each entry includes details on access, update schedule, content, reliability, coverage, licensing, and how the data is handled in YETO. The registry distinguishes global sources and Yemen national sources, and notes any special handling (e.g. Yemen’s dual authorities). Below, sources are grouped by type for clarity, with full details:

Global Economic & Trade Sources
	•	World Bank Open Data (Indicators) (World Bank):
	•	URL: https://api.worldbank.org/v2/country/YEM/indicator/{indicator_code}?format=json (REST API for World Development Indicators)
	•	Access Method: REST API (no key required)
	•	Authentication: None
	•	Update Cadence: Monthly, Quarterly, Annually (varies by indicator)
	•	Data Fields Available: Country, Indicator Code/Name, Year/Period, Value, Metadata (units, notes)
	•	Regime Split Handling: Not applicable (unified country dataset)
	•	Licensing/Terms: Open Data (CC-BY 4.0)
	•	Reliability Score: A (highly credible official data source)
	•	Coverage Type: Extensive national time-series indicators (1960–present); national-level data only
	•	Known Caveats: Some series have gaps or model-estimated values during conflict years; indicator definitions may change over time
	•	Mapped Sectors & Pages: Sectors – Macroeconomic & Trade Indicators (مؤشرات الاقتصاد الكلي والتجارة); Pages – Macro Trends Dashboard, Governance Index, Scenario Simulator, Data Explorer API, Methodology
	•	Ingestion Method: Direct API connector (JSON pagination); scheduled pull of updated indicator values daily/weekly based on series frequency; automatic parsing into time-series tables
	•	Fallbacks: If API fails or shows no new data by expected date, system retries with backoff. If still no update beyond schedule, an ingestion alert is raised and a Data Gap Ticket is generated. (No alternative source for WDI, but overlapping indicators from IMF or national sources may be considered if World Bank data is outdated)
	•	IMF Data (SDMX/IFS, Article IV) (International Monetary Fund):
	•	URL: SDMX API endpoints (e.g. https://sdmx.imf.org/rest/data/IFS/... for IFS dataset) and periodic Article IV PDF reports
	•	Access Method: API (SDMX XML/JSON) for International Financial Statistics and other IMF datasets; Article IV reports via PDF download
	•	Authentication: API key may be required for large-volume SDMX queries (free registration)
	•	Update Cadence: Quarterly (IFS and other macro datasets); Monthly (selected series); Annual (Article IV reports)
	•	Data Fields Available: Country, Indicator Code, Period (quarter/month/year), Value; Article IV PDFs contain narrative and projections
	•	Regime Split Handling: Not applicable (unified dataset for Yemen, though post-2015 data may be estimated due to limited official reporting)
	•	Licensing/Terms: Free with attribution; some data (Article IV content) may have reuse restrictions for text
	•	Reliability Score: A– (authoritative, but data for recent years can be partial or IMF-estimated)
	•	Coverage Type: National macro-financial time series (e.g. GDP, inflation, money supply, FX reserves, government finance) from 2010–present; includes historical estimates where official data is missing
	•	Known Caveats: National-level data only; missing recent observations due to conflict – IMF may use modeled estimates. Article IV projections are subject to revision
	•	Mapped Sectors & Pages: Sectors – Macroeconomic & Financial (الاقتصاد الكلي والقطاع المالي); Pages – Macro Trends, Financial Sector Dashboard, Public Finance, Scenario Simulator, Document Library (for reports), Glossary
	•	Ingestion Method: Build an SDMX API client to pull IMF data (e.g. quarterly IFS series); parse XML/JSON into YETO’s time-series schema. Also ingest Article IV PDFs into the document repository (with text extraction for search)
	•	Fallbacks: If API calls fail (e.g. due to key issues), the system retries later. Persistent failures or missing recent data trigger admin notification to check credentials or obtain the data via the Article IV PDF manually. If a particular indicator is not updated beyond expected lag, YETO flags it and creates a Gap Ticket (e.g. to seek data from Yemeni sources or latest IMF staff estimates)
	•	UN Comtrade (UN Statistics Division – Comtrade):
	•	URL: REST API (JSON/CSV), e.g. https://comtrade.un.org/api/get?max=50000&type=C&freq=A&px=HS&cc=ALL&r=887 (API query for Yemen [country code 887])
	•	Access Method: REST API for merchandise trade data; supports annual (freq=A) and monthly (freq=M) trade flows. Rate limiting in place for large queries
	•	Authentication: No API key needed for moderate use (registration required for high-volume access)
	•	Update Cadence: Monthly (preliminary monthly trade), Annual (detailed yearly trade statistics)
	•	Data Fields Available: Trade flow (import/export), period (year or month), reporter country, partner country, commodity code (HS), commodity description, trade value, quantity
	•	Regime Split Handling: Not applicable (unified national trade data; if Yemen does not report, partner data (“mirror data”) is used)
	•	Licensing/Terms: Open for non-commercial use with attribution
	•	Reliability Score: B+ (generally reliable, though mirror data is used when Yemen’s own reporting is absent)
	•	Coverage Type: Merchandise trade statistics by commodity and trading partner; 2010–present. Uses mirror data for years Yemen stopped reporting due to conflict
	•	Known Caveats: National totals only (no subnational breakdown). Gaps in Yemen-reported data for conflict years; partner-reported data may omit informal trade. Large queries require pagination due to API limits
	•	Mapped Sectors & Pages: Sectors – Trade & External (التجارة والقطاع الخارجي); Pages – Trade & Commerce Dashboard, Macro Trends, Regional Comparison modules
	•	Ingestion Method: API connector with batch queries. The pipeline fetches annual data (and monthly if available) in CSV/JSON, handles rate limits and large data by paging through results, and loads into YETO trade tables
	•	Fallbacks: If API returns errors or rate-limit is hit, the system waits and retries. If Yemen-origin data is unavailable for a period, the pipeline automatically falls back to using partner countries’ data as proxy (mirror data), flagged accordingly. Continued API issues trigger an alert for admin and a Gap Ticket. (UN Comtrade also offers bulk downloads as a backup if the API is down)
	•	UNCTADstat (UN Conference on Trade and Development):
	•	URL: UNCTADstat portal (no open API). Bulk data available via downloadable Excel/CSV from UNCTADstat website
	•	Access Method: Bulk file download (Excel/CSV) for indicators like FDI flows, external debt, commodities indices. Some datasets require site registration/login
	•	Authentication: Registration required for certain dataset downloads (otherwise public for most data)
	•	Update Cadence: Annual updates (e.g. yearly FDI and external debt stats); commodity price indices updated monthly/quarterly
	•	Data Fields Available: Indicator, country, year (or quarter), value (e.g. FDI inflow USD, external debt as % GDP, commodity price index values)
	•	Regime Split Handling: Not applicable (national-level data)
	•	Licensing/Terms: Open data for analysis with attribution (UNCTAD sources)
	•	Reliability Score: B+ (credible UN source; may have moderate lag in updates)
	•	Coverage Type: Trade and development indicators complementary to Comtrade (e.g. services trade, investment) for 2010–present; national aggregates
	•	Known Caveats: Data provided at national level, updated with significant delay (often 1+ year lag). Some series might stop after war onset due to reporting gaps. Users must interpret definitions carefully (FDI vs aid, etc.)
	•	Mapped Sectors & Pages: Sectors – Trade & Development (التجارة والتنمية); Pages – Macro Trends, Investment Dashboard, Research Hub
	•	Ingestion Method: Manual or scripted bulk download from UNCTADstat site. ETL script parses Excel/CSV files and ingests into YETO’s time-series database. Annual job checks for new files and updates relevant indicators
	•	Fallbacks: If the official download is unavailable or the format changes, ingestion flags an error. The system will alert an admin to manually retrieve data or update credentials. Missing yearly updates beyond the expected schedule trigger a Gap Ticket (e.g., if the latest FDI data is delayed, YETO will prompt to check UNCTAD or find alternate sources like World Bank)
	•	ILOSTAT (International Labour Organization):
	•	URL: https://api.ilo.org/v1/data/YE?[...] (ILO STAT API for Yemen, requires key)
	•	Access Method: REST API (ILO’s JSON data API) for labor force indicators; also data downloads on ILOSTAT website
	•	Authentication: API key (free registration with ILO) required for API access
	•	Update Cadence: Annual (most labor force indicators updated yearly); some modelled estimates updated as needed
	•	Data Fields Available: Indicator (e.g. unemployment rate, labor force participation), sex/age breakdown, year, value; possibly quarterly for few series.
	•	Regime Split Handling: Not applicable (national statistics, occasionally urban/rural breakdown but not by political regime)
	•	Licensing/Terms: Open data with attribution to ILO
	•	Reliability Score: A– (internationally vetted data; estimates used when official data lacking)
	•	Coverage Type: Labor market and socio-economic indicators (employment, unemployment, youth NEET rate, wages, etc.) for 2010–present (modeled values for conflict years post-2015)
	•	Known Caveats: National-level; data for recent years may be ILO estimates due to Yemen’s statistical disruption. Some indicators may not reflect informal employment accurately
	•	Mapped Sectors & Pages: Sectors – Socio-economic (Labor) (اجتماعية-اقتصادية (العمالة)); Pages – Macro & Social Trends, Research Hub, Glossary (labor definitions)
	•	Ingestion Method: API client pulls annual indicator data (with disaggregations) for Yemen. The ETL process merges any new data, ensuring consistent indicator codes. Missing official data points are left blank or filled with ILO modelled estimates (flagged as such in provenance)
	•	Fallbacks: If the ILO API is unreachable or not updated, the system retries. After continued failure or if the new year’s data doesn’t appear when expected, an ingestion alert is sent. A Gap Ticket is created to either follow up with ILO or switch to alternate sources (e.g. World Bank’s modeled unemployment) until ILO updates resume. Admin can also do a one-off manual download from ILOSTAT site if needed
	•	FAO – FAOSTAT & Food Security (UN Food & Agriculture Organization):
	•	URL: FAOSTAT web portal (bulk CSV download), and FAO Food Security data (e.g. Food Price Monitoring datasets)
	•	Access Method: Bulk data downloads (CSV/Excel) from FAOSTAT; no API for older FAOSTAT, but some datasets accessible via API. Data updated annually; some price data monthly
	•	Authentication: None (public downloads)
	•	Update Cadence: Annual for production/crop datasets; more frequent for price indices or Food Security Monitoring bulletins
	•	Data Fields Available: Agriculture production volumes, livestock counts, food supply (quantities, calories), commodity prices, Food Security Indicators by year, etc.
	•	Regime Split Handling: Not applicable (national totals; no political split)
	•	Licensing/Terms: Open data (FAO). Attribution required
	•	Reliability Score: A (FAO is authoritative for agricultural data; though Yemen data may have gaps)
	•	Coverage Type: National agriculture and food supply metrics, and market price indicators; covers 2010–present. Some subnational data in food security assessments (when available)
	•	Known Caveats: Data can have gaps due to conflict (e.g. some years missing for crop production). Some figures are estimates or from partner surveys. Inconsistencies may exist between FAO and national Ministry data
	•	Mapped Sectors & Pages: Sectors – Agriculture/Food (الزراعة والغذاء); Pages – Macro Trends, Markets & Prices, Aid & Food Security Dashboard, Research Hub
	•	Ingestion Method: ETL script for FAOSTAT bulk files – downloads latest CSVs for Yemen, transforms them to YETO schema (e.g. annual cereal production). Also ingests monthly Food Price Index or similar if provided. Integrates with WFP price data for a comprehensive food security view
	•	Fallbacks: If FAO data files are not updated or download fails, the system logs an error and tries again next cycle. Prolonged lack of updates triggers an alert to data admins. A Data Gap Ticket is issued for missing critical data (e.g. if annual crop output data is skipped during conflict years, mark as gap and potentially seek estimations from WFP or FEWSNET). There’s no alternate automated source, so manual entry or partner data might be needed if FAO remains unavailable

Humanitarian & Development Data Sources
	•	UNOCHA Financial Tracking Service (FTS) (UN OCHA):
	•	URL: OCHA HPC/FTS API – e.g. https://api.hpc.tools/v2/public/fts/flow?countryISO3=YEM for Yemen funding flows
	•	Access Method: REST API (public, no key required) for humanitarian funding data
	•	Authentication: None
	•	Update Cadence: Daily (data is updated in real-time as pledges/allocations are recorded)
	•	Data Fields Available: Funding flows: donor, recipient agency, destination country (Yemen), year, amount (commitment/paid), funding status, aid sectors/clusters, etc. Also appeals and requirements by year
	•	Regime Split Handling: Not applicable (funding data is nationwide or project-specific; not split by de facto authorities)
	•	Licensing/Terms: Open data (public domain humanitarian data)
	•	Reliability Score: A (official UN tracking system for aid; near-real-time updates)
	•	Coverage Type: Humanitarian aid financial flows for Yemen, including all donor contributions and allocations, 2010–present. Covers global appeals and Yemen Humanitarian Response Plan funding
	•	Known Caveats: Data reflects reported funding only – there may be unreported bilateral aid. Also, prior to 2015, data is aggregated; after 2015, detailed project-level entries. Occasional duplicates or revisions when funding is reallocated
	•	Mapped Sectors & Pages: Sectors – Humanitarian Aid Flows (تدفقات المساعدات الإنسانية); Pages – Aid Funding Dashboard, Donor Profiles, Cluster/Sector Funding pages, Crisis Timeline, AI Assistant (for funding queries)
	•	Ingestion Method: Daily API ingestion job. Fetches latest funding records (or deltas) for Yemen from HPC Tools API. Normalizes into YETO schema (donor, recipient, amount, etc.), linking to appeal ID and cluster. Summaries for total funding vs requirements are calculated for dashboards
	•	Fallbacks: If the FTS API is unreachable or returns errors, YETO automatically retries. If no data comes through beyond the expected short lag, an alert is raised. Since OCHA FTS data is critical, a failure triggers a Gap Ticket. As a backup, YETO can use the last cached data or try the HDX mirror of FTS if available. Prolonged outage would prompt contacting OCHA or ingesting funding data from manual reports
	•	International Aid Transparency Initiative (IATI) (IATI Secretariat):
	•	URL: IATI Datastore API or CSV downloads (e.g. https://iati.cloud/api/activities/?recipient_country=YE for Yemen activities)
	•	Access Method: IATI Datastore API (open), and bulk XML datasets from IATI registry
	•	Authentication: None (public data)
	•	Update Cadence: Weekly updates to the datastore (YETO will fetch new activities weekly)
	•	Data Fields Available: Aid project activities with detailed fields: IATI identifier, reporting org, participating orgs, sector, geographic location, budget and expenditures, transaction amounts (commitment/disbursement), dates, descriptions
	•	Regime Split Handling: Not applicable (projects are coded for Yemen overall or specific regions, but not distinguished by regime in data; YETO can filter by location if needed)
	•	Licensing/Terms: Open data (publishers agree to open license)
	•	Reliability Score: A– (comprehensive, but depends on donors/NGOs updating data; some data can be outdated or incomplete)
	•	Coverage Type: Development & humanitarian project activities in Yemen, 2010–present; includes thousands of records from various donors/NGOs (covers project-level financials and results)
	•	Known Caveats: Data quality varies by publisher. There may be duplicates between IATI and FTS for humanitarian projects. Some projects lack geolocation or results info. Data is as reported by organizations, not verified by a single authority
	•	Mapped Sectors & Pages: Sectors – Development & Humanitarian Projects (مشاريع التنمية والمساعدات الإنسانية); Pages – Aid Projects Dashboard, Stakeholder (Donor/NGO) Profiles, Geospatial Project Map, AI Assistant (for querying project data)
	•	Ingestion Method: Weekly ETL job queries IATI’s API for activities where country = Yemen (or uses the bulk XML if more efficient). The pipeline parses XML/JSON into YETO’s project database, linking projects with sectors, locations, and financial transactions. It flags any new or updated activities each run
	•	Fallbacks: If the IATI API is slow or down, YETO will retry with backoff. Missing updates beyond a week triggers an alert; if needed, a one-time bulk download from the IATI registry can be used as a fallback. Persistent API issues generate a Gap Ticket so that data engineers can investigate or switch to the datastore CSV dumps. (The system ensures that if IATI data is unavailable, at minimum the last known dataset remains accessible)
	•	ReliefWeb API (Reports) (UN OCHA ReliefWeb):
	•	URL: https://api.reliefweb.int/v1/reports?appname=yeto&query[country]=yemen (ReliefWeb REST API for reports filtered by country)
	•	Access Method: REST API returning recent reports, analyses, and maps related to Yemen
	•	Authentication: None (open API, optional API key for higher rate limit)
	•	Update Cadence: Daily (ReliefWeb content updates continuously; YETO fetches new entries daily)
	•	Data Fields Available: Report metadata – title, publication date, source organization, themes, summary, URLs to full text or PDF
	•	Regime Split Handling: Not applicable (humanitarian reports are narrative, covering all of Yemen or regions, not by political regime)
	•	Licensing/Terms: Open; content is public domain or under original source’s terms. Metadata and abstracts are open
	•	Reliability Score: A
	•	Coverage Type: All humanitarian situation reports, analyses, infographics, etc., related to Yemen on ReliefWeb; 2010–present archive accessible
	•	Known Caveats: Largely unstructured text content; no numeric data consistency. Large volume of documents – requires filtering for relevance (economic-related content vs general crisis reports). Some older PDFs might require OCR for full text search
	•	Mapped Sectors & Pages: Sectors – Humanitarian Information (Media/Reports) (المعلومات الإنسانية (تقارير/إعلام)); Pages – Research Hub (library of reports), Timeline, AI Assistant (for answering questions from report content), Glossary (linking terms)
	•	Ingestion Method: Daily API ingest of new reports. YETO stores metadata and fetches the full text or PDF for each new report. Documents are added to the searchable Research Library, and relevant tags (themes, organizations) are stored. The content is also vector-indexed for semantic search by the AI
	•	Fallbacks: If the ReliefWeb API fails on a given day, the system will retry. Since new content appears almost daily, any API downtime beyond 24 hours triggers an alert to check the API status. A persistent issue would create a Gap Ticket. As a backup, YETO could use ReliefWeb’s RSS feeds or web-scrape new reports (if permitted) until the API is restored. Missing documents can also be manually uploaded by admins if needed
	•	UNDP/UNICEF/WFP/OCHA Public Reports & Data (Various UN Agencies – Yemen):
	•	URL: Multiple sources (e.g. UNDP Yemen economic reports on undp.org, UNICEF Yemen statistics, WFP DataViz portal for Yemen, OCHA Humanitarian Data Exchange for Yemen datasets)
	•	Access Method: Manual downloads of PDFs, Excel sheets, or via agency public data portals (no unified API)
	•	Authentication: None for public reports (some internal datasets require permission, but YETO uses public-facing data)
	•	Update Cadence: Occasional – typically quarterly or annual publications (e.g. UNDP development updates, Joint UN agency assessment reports, etc.)
	•	Data Fields Available: Various, depending on report – could include poverty rates, population in need, food security assessment figures, development indicators, etc., alongside narrative analysis
	•	Regime Split Handling: Not applicable (data usually presented at national level or governorate level, but as part of unified humanitarian/development analysis)
	•	Licensing/Terms: Public domain or Creative Commons (most UN publications). Data intended for public use with attribution
	•	Reliability Score: A– (high credibility, but data may be infrequent or not systematic)
	•	Coverage Type: Policy briefs, needs assessments, socio-economic impact reports, etc., covering Yemen’s development and humanitarian context; 2010–present (with more frequent reports post-2015)
	•	Known Caveats: Indicators in these reports may not be regularly updated or consistent across agencies. Some data might overlap with official stats or other sources. Coverage can be patchy (e.g. poverty stats might come from old surveys)
	•	Mapped Sectors & Pages: Sectors – Development & Humanitarian Analysis (التحليلات التنموية والإنسانية); Pages – Humanitarian Overview, Poverty & Social Indicators, Research Hub, AI Assistant (for Q&A on these reports)
	•	Ingestion Method: Manual ingestion pipeline: whenever a new UN agency report is published, it is downloaded (PDF or data file) and added to YETO. Key tables or data points are extracted (through manual or semi-automated parsing) for structured use, while the full document text is stored and indexed. YETO flags upcoming annual reports (e.g. Human Development Reports) and checks those sources periodically
	•	Fallbacks: Since there’s no set schedule, if an expected report (e.g. an annual UNDP update) is not published by a usual date, the system flags it for manual follow-up. For ingestion, if a PDF is scanned or not parseable, YETO prompts a manual data entry or OCR. Any critical dataset not updated triggers a Gap Ticket (for example, if a yearly humanitarian needs assessment is missing, to coordinate obtaining that data through partners)
	•	WFP Yemen Market & Price Monitoring (World Food Programme – VAM):
	•	URL: WFP Vulnerability Analysis and Mapping (VAM) data portal (Yemen country page), and Humanitarian Data Exchange (HDX) for Yemen price data. Monthly price bulletins are PDFs; raw data often available in CSV/Excel
	•	Access Method: Combination – manual parsing of PDF reports, plus CSV/Excel downloads when provided. (WFP’s API is limited, so much is manual)
	•	Authentication: None (public reports)
	•	Update Cadence: Monthly reports (market monitor); some raw price data bi-weekly or monthly
	•	Data Fields Available: Commodity prices (e.g. wheat flour, rice, fuel) by market and governorate, unit of measure, Yemeni Rial price; cost of minimum food basket; exchange rate (official vs market) trends; dates of observation
	•	Regime Split Handling: Not applicable (WFP reports typically aggregate national trends and regional differences, but do not label by political regime – though they implicitly cover both controlled areas)
	•	Licensing/Terms: Open data for humanitarian use, attribution to WFP VAM
	•	Reliability Score: A (primary on-ground data source for prices; collected by partners)
	•	Coverage Type: Subnational market price time series (covering key cities in governorates across Yemen); also national indices. Data from ~2010–present (with gaps during intense conflict periods)
	•	Known Caveats: Gaps for some regions during conflict peaks. Prices in Houthi-controlled vs GoY areas can differ significantly – WFP reports note these but dataset itself needs careful filtering by city. Not all commodities covered in all periods. Potential lag in releasing reports (data is usually a few weeks old when published)
	•	Mapped Sectors & Pages: Sectors – Market Prices & Food Security (أسعار السوق والأمن الغذائي); Pages – FX & Inflation Monitor (for exchange rates/inflation proxies), Food Security Panel, Humanitarian Planning Dashboard, Timeline
	•	Ingestion Method: A custom parser reads the PDF reports each month, extracting price tables. When WFP provides an accompanying CSV (sometimes on HDX), that is ingested directly for higher accuracy. Data is stored in a “market_prices” time-series table keyed by location and commodity. The pipeline also calculates derived indicators like monthly inflation from these price series
	•	Fallbacks: If a monthly report is delayed or not found, YETO issues an alert to check WFP’s site. If parsing fails (due to format changes or poor PDF quality), the job flags an error for manual intervention. Missing price updates beyond one cycle create a Gap Ticket so that the team can seek the data (possibly via WFP contacts or alternative sources). In a pinch, last available prices remain on the platform marked as “latest” until new data arrives
	•	Fuel Price Bulletins & Partner Feeds (Yemeni fuel companies & clusters):
	•	URL: No formal API – data comes from monthly fuel price bulletins (PDFs) issued by Yemeni authorities or humanitarian clusters, and direct partner submissions via email or spreadsheets
	•	Access Method: Manual data entry and ingestion from bulletins/announcements; some semi-structured partner feeds (e.g. cluster coordinators sharing price updates)
	•	Authentication: None for publicly posted bulletins; partner data via trust arrangement (no public credentials)
	•	Update Cadence: Ad-hoc, roughly monthly (especially via the Logistics Cluster or Fuel Task Force)
	•	Data Fields Available: Date of price observation, region/area (typically distinguishing GoY-controlled vs DFA-controlled areas), fuel type (petrol, diesel, cooking gas), price per liter (or per gas cylinder) in YER
	•	Regime Split Handling: Yes – data is explicitly split by authority in many cases (separate price for north vs south regions)
	•	Licensing/Terms: Public domain or shared within humanitarian community (with consent to use for analysis)
	•	Reliability Score: B (data collected from local sources; generally accurate but not always timely or comprehensive)
	•	Coverage Type: Regional pricing – usually at least two sets of prices (north and south Yemen), sometimes further broken by city. Covers 2010–present in patches (consistent data collection post-2016)
	•	Known Caveats: Regional disparities: official set prices vs black-market prices vary widely, especially during crises. The bulletins might not capture unofficial market spikes. Data can be missing in some months or requires triangulation with news reports
	•	Mapped Sectors & Pages: Sectors – Market Prices (أسعار السوق); Pages – Markets & Prices Dashboard, Fuel Subsidy Tracker, Timeline, AI Assistant (for answering cost of living questions)
	•	Ingestion Method: A structured template is used for partners to submit monthly price data (e.g. via Google Sheets or CSV). The ingestion pipeline either ingests these submissions or a YETO analyst enters the bulletin data into the system. Data is stored with a region tag (North/South) to allow separate tracking. Any new bulletins trigger an update job to insert the latest prices
	•	Fallbacks: If expected monthly data isn’t received, YETO flags this for follow-up with the data providers (e.g. cluster leads). The system will carry forward the last known prices marked as outdated. Continued absence triggers a Data Gap Ticket. No automated alternate source exists, but if the official bulletin is unavailable, YETO will attempt to gather prices from media or NGO reports and document the provenance accordingly
	•	UNHCR/IOM Population & Displacement Data (UNHCR & IOM):
	•	URL: UNHCR Population Statistics API (https://api.unhcr.org/population/v1/), and IOM Displacement Tracking Matrix (DTM) Yemen datasets (available via IOM portal or CSV)
	•	Access Method: UNHCR – open API for refugee/asylum data; IOM – manual download of Excel/CSV reports (no open API for Yemen DTM)
	•	Authentication: UNHCR API requires no auth (public); IOM DTM data access may require signup or direct request if not on public sites
	•	Update Cadence: UNHCR – Annual update (refugees, asylum-seekers by year); IOM – Irregular (DTM rounds conducted periodically, roughly quarterly or ad-hoc when displacement surges)
	•	Data Fields Available: UNHCR: Number of refugees/from Yemen, asylum seekers, etc., by country of asylum/origin, year, demographic breakdown. IOM: Number of internally displaced persons (IDPs), returnees, by governorate/district, site assessments, needs metrics per location
	•	Regime Split Handling: Not applicable in data – population stats cover the whole country or specific governorates; they are not categorized by north/south authority (though IOM data is subnational)
	•	Licensing/Terms: Open data for humanitarian use (attribution to UNHCR/IOM)
	•	Reliability Score: B (data collected via large-scale surveys and registration – generally good, but some uncertainty in conflict zones)
	•	Coverage Type: Population movements: Refugees/ asylum (Yemenis abroad and refugees in Yemen) since 2010; Internal displacement: IDP counts and returnee counts inside Yemen, mainly post-2015 conflict period. Data spans 2010–present, with significant displacement tracking from 2015 onward
	•	Known Caveats: UNHCR data is annual and might lag a year. IOM’s DTM covers accessible districts – some areas may be inaccessible leading to undercounts. Figures can quickly become outdated due to ongoing conflict displacement
	•	Mapped Sectors & Pages: Sectors – Humanitarian – Population/Movement (السكان والنزوح الإنساني); Pages – Humanitarian Dashboard (displacement and refugee statistics), Stakeholder Profiles (for UNHCR/IOM), Scenario Simulator (to model population movements)
	•	Ingestion Method: The UNHCR API is polled annually to update refugee/asylum figures (broken down by origin/destination). Data is stored in YETO’s population stats table. For IOM, whenever a new DTM report is released (new round), an ingestion job (manual or semi-automated) loads the CSV of IDP counts by location. Subnational data is stored with admin area codes for mapping and analysis
	•	Fallbacks: If the UNHCR API fails or hasn’t updated a new year’s data, YETO will continue to use the last data and mark the delay. After expected update time, an alert triggers a Gap Ticket (though typically UNHCR updates annually mid-year). For IOM, if new displacement reports are not shared on schedule, the system flags it for the cluster coordinators. Any failure in parsing an IOM file (format changes) raises an error to update the parser. Persistent lack of updates (e.g. no new DTM in a year) will create a Gap Ticket to consider alternate IDP data sources (like UNHCR or protection cluster estimates)

Conflict & Security Sources
	•	ACLED (Armed Conflict Location & Event Data) (ACLED):
	•	URL: https://api.acleddata.com/acled/read?country=Yemen&year=2023 (ACLED API for Yemen events; requires API key for full access)
	•	Access Method: REST API and weekly CSV exports (ACLED database – licensed dataset)
	•	Authentication: Yes – API token or academic license required for full data access
	•	Update Cadence: Weekly updates (conflict events are added weekly; data may be revised periodically)
	•	Data Fields Available: Conflict event records: unique event ID, date, event type (battle, protest, airstrike, etc.), sub-event type, actors (actor1, actor2), locations (admin levels + coordinates), fatalities, source of information for the event
	•	Regime Split Handling: Not applicable (events are recorded individually with precise locations; the dataset doesn’t aggregate by political regime, though location indicates de facto control)
	•	Licensing/Terms: Restricted – ACLED data is free for academic/non-profit use with attribution but requires agreement; commercial use is restricted. Must credit ACLED in any use
	•	Reliability Score: A– (ACLED is a standard reference for conflict events; very detailed, but relies on reported info which may have verification limits)
	•	Coverage Type: Geospatial event data – every conflict incident logged with date and location. High granularity (village-level) covering 2015–present (ACLED Yemen data starts from the escalation of conflict; some retrospective data covers 2011–2014 at lower detail)
	•	Known Caveats: Casualty counts are estimates and can be disputed. ACLED might under-report in areas with low media coverage. Licensing means YETO can only use data for non-commercial/public-interest aspects and must suppress if license not granted. Data volume is large, requiring indexing for performance
	•	Mapped Sectors & Pages: Sectors – Conflict Events (أحداث الصراع); Pages – Interactive Conflict Map & Timeline, Security Incident Maps, AI Evidence Base (for conflict queries), Sanctions/Compliance (to contextualize security events)
	•	Ingestion Method: If licensed, YETO runs a weekly job to pull new Yemen events via the ACLED API or downloads the latest CSV for Yemen. Events are upserted into a dedicated conflict_events table with spatial coordinates. The system also generates summary stats (e.g. monthly incident counts) for dashboard visuals. The data is indexed for geospatial queries and time filtering
	•	Fallbacks: If API access is lost (e.g. license expires or token fails), YETO stops automated updates and notifies admins to renew credentials. The pipeline will retry with backoff for transient errors. If no update occurs in a weekly cycle (and ACLED is expected to have new data), an ingestion alert and Gap Ticket are created. License fallback: If ACLED licensing prevents data sharing, YETO will mark the conflict dataset as restricted; only aggregate figures may be shown until resolved. In case of extended API downtime, an alternative is to use ACLED’s last available dataset (stale data) and flag it, or switch to other conflict data like UCDP for basic trends
	•	UCDP (Uppsala Conflict Data Program) (Uppsala University):
	•	URL: https://ucdpapi.pcr.uu.se/api/gedevents/22.1?Country=YR (example API for UCDP GED events dataset v22.1 filtered for Yemen)
	•	Access Method: REST API (free, open) or bulk downloads for UCDP datasets (GED – battle-related deaths, etc.)
	•	Authentication: None (open access)
	•	Update Cadence: Annual release (the UCDP GED dataset is updated yearly with prior year’s data)
	•	Data Fields Available: Aggregated conflict data per event or per year: conflict identifier, year, number of fatalities, type of conflict (state-based, non-state, one-sided violence), locations (often country or region level), actors
	•	Regime Split Handling: Not applicable (data is country-level or broad regional for conflict events)
	•	Licensing/Terms: Free for non-commercial use; must cite UCDP version when used
	•	Reliability Score: B+ (academically rigorous, but less granular and slower update cycle than ACLED)
	•	Coverage Type: Conflict casualty statistics and events summary for Yemen from 2010–present, updated through the previous calendar year. Typically provides annual fatality counts and the number of incidents by conflict type
	•	Known Caveats: Less granular than ACLED – UCDP may report yearly totals rather than individual events. There is a time lag (data released mid-year for the prior year). Definitions may differ (e.g., what constitutes a conflict event vs ACLED’s definitions)
	•	Mapped Sectors & Pages: Sectors – Conflict Casualties (ضحايا الصراع); Pages – Conflict Overview Dashboard (with yearly casualty charts), Timeline (for conflict intensity), Research Hub (for conflict data downloads)
	•	Ingestion Method: An annual ingestion job pulls the latest UCDP GED dataset via API or download when released (usually by mid-year). The pipeline updates the conflict summary table (e.g., total fatalities per year, conflict type breakdown). This provides a cross-check against ACLED trends and a long-term view from 2010 onward
	•	Fallbacks: If the UCDP API is unavailable or the new yearly data is delayed, YETO continues showing the last release and flags the delay. After expected release month passes, an alert/gap ticket prompts checking UCDP’s website for the new dataset manually. Because UCDP is annual, short-term API issues are not critical; however, any schema changes or versioning issues (e.g. new API version) would be detected by the pipeline and require adjustments (which the system flags for developers)
	•	Yemen Data Project (Airstrikes) (Yemen Data Project):
	•	URL: No public API. Data obtained via YDP’s published reports or upon request (monthly airstrike summaries available on their website or via email subscription)
	•	Access Method: Manual retrieval – YDP publishes monthly statistics of air raids (often in infographics or reports). YETO either scrapes these from reports or receives data directly through partnerships
	•	Authentication: None for public summaries; direct data sharing might be done via email (requires relationship with YDP)
	•	Update Cadence: Monthly updates (airstrike counts by month) with an annual summary each year
	•	Data Fields Available: Month and year, number of airstrikes (sorties) recorded, possibly breakdown by governorate or target type in some reports; cumulative totals and graphs in annual reports
	•	Regime Split Handling: Not applicable (focus is on Saudi-led coalition air war; data inherently pertains to conflict actors rather than Yemeni regimes)
	•	Licensing/Terms: Attribution required; data is often shared for advocacy and research purposes freely, but the full dataset may be proprietary beyond published figures
	•	Reliability Score: A (widely cited source for airstrike data; methodology is consistent, though not officially “confirmed” by combatants)
	•	Coverage Type: Monthly count of airstrikes in Yemen from March 2015–present; includes nationwide total and sometimes regional splits (north vs south or specific governorates) in published materials
	•	Known Caveats: Data limited to air war; does not cover ground conflict or artillery. There may be revisions if new info emerges, but YDP tries to maintain consistent records. During lulls or ceasefires, “zero” events are as important to record. Also, if YDP ever ceases public updates, data flow could stop
	•	Mapped Sectors & Pages: Sectors – Conflict – Air War (الصراع – الحرب الجوية); Pages – Conflict Timeline (overlay of airstrike frequency), AI Evidence (for specific conflict questions), Compliance/Alerts (e.g., to highlight escalation periods)
	•	Ingestion Method: Manual/semi-automated. Each month, YETO staff obtain the latest airstrike figure. If YDP provides a CSV or structured data, it’s ingested directly; otherwise the number is extracted from YDP’s published infographic/report and input into the system. These monthly data points populate a time-series table of airstrikes, which feeds visualizations and analysis tools
	•	Fallbacks: If a monthly update is not published on time, the system alerts the team to check YDP communications. In absence of data, YETO will leave that month as “Not available” and create a Gap Ticket to follow up with YDP. Since YDP data is unique, there’s no direct alternative; however, if needed, YETO could use ACLED’s count of airstrike events as a temporary proxy (with clear caveats). For ingestion, if the format of YDP’s release changes (e.g., moved to a new website), a one-time scraper update or manual entry will be done as flagged by the pipeline

National Institutions & Financial Data Sources
	•	Central Bank of Yemen – Aden & Sana’a (National) (Central Bank of Yemen):
	•	URL: Official CBY Aden website (cby-aden.com) for bulletins and auction results; CBY Sana’a releases via Yemeni news or Ministry of Finance in Sana’a. Also CBY Facebook pages for announcements
	•	Access Method: Manual ingestion of public reports, auction result documents, and announcements (no unified API; data fragmented between Aden and Sana’a branches)
	•	Authentication: None (public releases); internal data would require agreements not currently in place
	•	Update Cadence: Weekly for FX auction results (Aden CBY); ad-hoc for circulars, exchange rate decisions, or monetary bulletins from either branch
	•	Data Fields Available: Foreign exchange auction results (date, USD amount sold, cut-off exchange rate, weighted average rate), official exchange rates, money supply aggregates (if published), key interest rates, lists of licensed banks/exchangers, and financial circulars text
	•	Regime Split Handling: Yes – the data is split by two authorities post-2016. The CBY in Aden vs CBY in Sana’a often issue separate and sometimes conflicting figures (e.g., different official exchange rates). YETO treats them as separate data streams with clear labels
	•	Licensing/Terms: Public domain (government data)
	•	Reliability Score: B– (data is official but often incomplete or published irregularly; potential bias or delayed reporting due to political issues)
	•	Coverage Type: National monetary indicators, but maintained separately by two central bank authorities. YETO covers 2010–present: unified data pre-2015, and dual-stream data thereafter (Aden vs Sana’a). No subnational granularity (national-level indicators)
	•	Known Caveats: Many data points are missing, especially during 2015–2017 gap. Some indicators (like money supply or inflation) may not be released by either branch in a timely fashion. Exchange rate info: official rates diverged (Aden vs Sana’a) from 2019 onward and must be handled carefully. Data needs context of who issued it
	•	Mapped Sectors & Pages: Sectors – Monetary & Financial Sector (القطاع النقدي والمالي); Pages – FX & Monetary Dashboard (official vs market rates, money supply), Banking Sector Overview, Timeline (major monetary policy events), AI Assistant (financial queries)
	•	Ingestion Method: Semi-automated + manual. A scheduled task each week checks the CBY Aden site for new auction result PDFs or announcements and scrapes relevant info (auction outcomes are often in tabular PDF format). For Sana’a, since official channels are opaque, YETO relies on partner inputs or scraping local news that publishes Sana’a CBY announcements. All data points are tagged with the issuing authority (Aden or Sana’a) in the database. The system also logs the document sources in the provenance ledger for each entry (e.g., link to the PDF of the auction result or the text of a circular)
	•	Fallbacks: If no auction result is posted for a scheduled week, YETO flags it – possibly no auction occurred, but a Data Gap Ticket is created to confirm. For any CBY data not updated (e.g., Aden CBY stops publishing a certain series), the system alerts admins to obtain data via direct contact or find alternatives (like IMF’s country reports). If the CBY website is down, the ingestion will retry; extended downtime triggers an alert for manual retrieval via alternate means (such as asking Central Bank contacts or checking social media announcements). All missing or outdated fields are marked “Not available” rather than leaving stale data, to maintain transparency
	•	Ministry of Finance/Planning/CSO (Yemen) (Government Ministries – internationally recognized GoY and de facto authorities):
	•	URL: Official ministry websites (when functional), plus leaked or published budget documents and plans circulating online. (Examples: MoF Aden site for budget summaries, MoPIC plans on their portals, and Sana’a de facto government budget books via news sites)
	•	Access Method: Manual document collection and ingestion – budgets, fiscal statements, development plans in PDF/Excel as available. There is no API; requires hunting documents from websites or partners
	•	Authentication: None for publicly leaked docs. Some internal data would require special access (not assumed in YETO initial implementation)
	•	Update Cadence: Highly irregular. Ideally annual budgets and development plans, but in practice Yemen’s official budgets have been sporadic (e.g., GoY budget published some years, none in others; DFA budgets separately). Development plans (e.g. plans or poverty reduction strategies) also irregular
	•	Data Fields Available: Budget figures (revenues, expenditures broken down by category or sector, deficit, financing sources), actual fiscal outcomes if available, public debt stock, economic development plan targets, population and CPI stats from CSO (Central Statistical Org.) where available up to 2014
	•	Regime Split Handling: Yes – two distinct sets of data in recent years. GoY (Aden) vs DFA (Sana’a) have separate budget documents and economic plans. YETO captures both and labels them by authority and time period
	•	Licensing/Terms: Public domain (government data), though some documents are unofficially obtained
	•	Reliability Score: C+ (the data that exists is official but often outdated or incomplete; some figures are estimates or propaganda. Requires cross-verification with IMF/WB for credibility)
	•	Coverage Type: National public finance and planning data, 2010–present, but with major gaps. Pre-2014, CSO data provides official stats. Post-2015, coverage depends on whether either authority released information (e.g., Sana’a published budgets 2016–2019 unofficially; Aden resumed budgets 2018 onward). YETO stores whatever is available and highlights missing periods
	•	Known Caveats: Completeness: Many years have no official budget published publicly. Consistency: Different formats between authorities and over years. Accuracy: Economic projections in plans may be unrealistic. Use with caution and compare with IMF data. Currency valuation differences (Sana’a uses 250 YER/USD rate for its budget accounting in recent years vs Aden using market rate) can distort comparisons
	•	Mapped Sectors & Pages: Sectors – Public Finance & Economic Planning (المالية العامة والتخطيط الاقتصادي); Pages – Public Finance Dashboard (expenditure/revenue trends), Debt Tracker, Economic Plans & Vision pages, Research Library (for storing PDFs of budgets)
	•	Ingestion Method: Entirely manual ETL. Whenever a budget or official report is obtained, analysts enter the key figures into YETO’s public finance data model (e.g., a table for annual govt revenue by category, one for expenditures by sector, etc.). Documents are also stored for reference. The ingestion process includes recording metadata: which authority (GoY or DFA), official vs unofficial status, and the source file. The system is set to expect an annual budget for each authority and will create placeholder entries marked “not available” if none is obtained, to signal gaps
	•	Fallbacks: If a new fiscal year begins with no budget from an authority, YETO automatically creates a Data Gap Ticket after a reasonable wait (e.g., 3 months into the year) detailing the missing budget. Meanwhile, the platform will show “Not available” for that year’s budget data. For other data (like GDP or inflation if CSO isn’t issuing), YETO relies on international sources as a fallback (World Bank/IMF) and cites them instead, while flagging the absence of national data. Any documents that cannot be parsed (scanned PDFs) are flagged for manual data extraction. Essentially, the pipeline leans on external sources and manual entry to fill critical public finance indicators when official data is absent, all while documenting the provenance and gap status
	•	Social Fund for Development (SFD) (Social Fund for Development – Yemen):
	•	URL: SFD’s official website and publications section (for annual reports, project reports, etc.)
	•	Access Method: Manual download of PDF reports and evaluation documents; potential for direct data sharing via SFD if arranged (not assumed initially)
	•	Authentication: None for public reports. (Access to internal project databases would require an MoU, future possibility)
	•	Update Cadence: Annual reporting (SFD publishes an annual report with summary stats); plus occasional project monitoring reports. During conflict, updates may be less regular
	•	Data Fields Available: Number of projects funded, total disbursed amount, sectoral breakdown (education, health, water, etc.), number of beneficiaries, labor days created (cash-for-work), microfinance loan portfolios, etc., per year. Possibly project-level lists if available
	•	Regime Split Handling: Not applicable (SFD operates across Yemen as one entity, though activities may be constrained in conflict areas, the data is reported nationally)
	•	Licensing/Terms: Public information (reports). SFD is a government-affiliated entity but shares info openly in reports
	•	Reliability Score: A– (SFD is a well-regarded institution with strong monitoring, but during war some reporting might be delayed or partial)
	•	Coverage Type: Development project outputs and social program metrics nationwide. 2010–present (though data after 2015 sometimes summarized over multi-year periods due to war)
	•	Known Caveats: Data often aggregated yearly and by sector; microfinance network data included via SFD’s facilitation. Detailed project-level data might not be fully open. Also, overlaps with IATI/FTS data: some SFD projects funded by donors appear there too. Need to reconcile if double-counting in platform
	•	Mapped Sectors & Pages: Sectors – Development Projects (مشاريع التنمية); Pages – Aid Projects Dashboard (SFD projects appear here as government programs), Poverty & Resilience Indicators (impact metrics), Stakeholder Profile: SFD
	•	Ingestion Method: SFD’s annual report PDFs are ingested into YETO’s document store, and key figures (total projects, funds, beneficiaries, etc.) are pulled out and stored as time-series or categorical indicators. If available, the list of projects (with donor funding, status) is loaded, aligning with IATI project entries (to avoid duplication, YETO cross-references projects by name or ID). This is largely a manual ETL process given the format of SFD reporting
	•	Fallbacks: If SFD does not release a report for a year (or it’s not obtainable publicly), YETO will issue a Data Gap Ticket to reach out to SFD or monitor alternative communications (e.g., newsletters). In the interim, the platform notes the lack of new data. There is no alternative source for SFD aggregate figures (apart from piecemeal references in donor reports), so missing SFD data simply remains blank until acquired. For ingestion, any issues with parsing (e.g. tables in PDFs) are flagged for manual data entry by an administrator
	•	Yemen Microfinance Network (YMN) (Yemen Microfinance Network):
	•	URL: Publications from YMN (e.g. annual conference reports, bulletins). YMN is a network of microfinance institutions in Yemen, often supported by SFD
	•	Access Method: Manual collection of any available reports or data releases (no centralized public database)
	•	Authentication: N/A – data usually shared in public domain via reports or by request through SFD
	•	Update Cadence: In the past, quarterly or annual statistics (pre-conflict); post-2015, updates are irregular due to disruptions in the microfinance sector
	•	Data Fields Available: Number of active microfinance institutions (MFIs), active borrowers, active savers, total loan portfolio size, portfolio at risk (PAR>30), number of branches, and possibly financial statements aggregates. Sometimes disaggregated by governorate if provided
	•	Regime Split Handling: Not applicable (the network spans the whole country; data is aggregated nationally, although conflict may limit some MFIs operations)
	•	Licensing/Terms: Shared within development community; treat as public unless marked otherwise. Will attribute YMN/SMEPS**
	•	Reliability Score: B (valuable niche data, but not consistently updated and some MFIs might drop out of reporting during conflict)
	•	Coverage Type: Financial inclusion indicators and MFI performance data, 2010–present where available. Likely complete data up to 2014, then sparse info, with a few surveys post-2015 (e.g. YMN report in 2017 covering war impact)
	•	Known Caveats: Data may be outdated – e.g., portfolio size from 2017 could be the last available for years. The network’s capacity is limited in conflict, so data coverage is spotty. Use in context of trends rather than current exact figures
	•	Mapped Sectors & Pages: Sectors – Financial Inclusion (الشمول المالي); Pages – Finance & Inclusion Dashboard (microfinance indicators), Geographical Maps (if branch coverage can be mapped), Research Hub
	•	Ingestion Method: When YMN or related entities publish a report, the data is manually extracted. YETO might maintain a small table of key microfinance indicators by year (and by institution if details available). Some data can be cross-verified with SFD (since SFD’s Microfinance Unit often collates these). Because no automatic feed exists, ingestion is triggered by discovery of new info (via the dynamic discovery or manual checking of SFD/YMN updates)
	•	Fallbacks: In absence of recent data (which is likely), YETO continues to display the last known figures with a note on their date. The system will generate a Gap Ticket to seek updated microfinance info through SFD or donor programs if none has been obtained in over a year. If YMN publishing stops entirely, YETO may rely on anecdotal data (e.g., from World Bank financial inclusion surveys) as a placeholder, clearly marked. Essentially, this source requires proactive manual updates when possible, with the platform highlighting the data’s age
	•	Association of Yemeni Banks (AYB) (Association of Yemeni Banks):
	•	URL: No dedicated data portal. AYB sometimes releases statements or annual banking sector reviews (often via press or PDF bulletins shared among banks)
	•	Access Method: Manual – by collecting any available AYB publications or communications. YETO may rely on industry reports or media that cite AYB data
	•	Authentication: None (if data is published informally)
	•	Update Cadence: Ad-hoc. Possibly annual meetings might yield a summary of banking sector status (e.g. number of banks, total assets, issues faced). Not guaranteed every year
	•	Data Fields Available: Qualitative assessments of the banking sector, high-level aggregates (e.g., total deposits in the banking system, number of operating banks, bank branch counts), and notes on regulatory changes or compliance issues. Often narrative rather than structured data
	•	Regime Split Handling: Not applicable in data (banks network spans country; however, since 2016 the sector split regulatory oversight – but AYB likely addresses whole sector in general terms)
	•	Licensing/Terms: Not formally licensed; treat information as public domain if obtained from media/press releases
	•	Reliability Score: C (the information is useful but tends to be qualitative or partial; AYB is not a statistical agency. It may highlight issues rather than provide comprehensive data)
	•	Coverage Type: Banking sector insights covering all Yemen. Data from 2010s mostly narrative (e.g., banking conference outputs). YETO uses it for context rather than core time series
	•	Known Caveats: Lack of consistent numeric data series. Any figures given (like total bank assets) might not be regularly tracked by AYB or might exclude some banks. For robust banking data, one would also need CBY statistics (which are scarce). Thus AYB content is supplementary
	•	Mapped Sectors & Pages: Sectors – Banking Sector (القطاع المصرفي); Pages – Banking Sector Overview (qualitative context notes), Compliance Dashboard (if AYB provides any insight on regulations or compliance issues)
	•	Ingestion Method: YETO treats AYB inputs as stakeholder narrative. That is, if AYB releases a report or if an interview with AYB leadership reveals data, that text is ingested into the provenance ledger and document store (for search). Any concrete numbers (e.g., “only 4 out of 16 banks remain fully operational”) are logged as data points in a small reference table (stakeholder stats). In short, ingestion here is more unstructured: capturing statements and making them searchable, rather than a formal data pipeline
	•	Fallbacks: If no data or statements come from AYB, YETO simply may not show anything from this source (there are no expected regular updates, so no automated gap detection). However, if the platform has a placeholder for “Banking sector status” and it’s empty, the admin might create a Gap Ticket to consider reaching out to AYB or using other sources (like IMF reports) for banking info. Any promised publication from AYB that doesn’t materialize would similarly be noted as a gap. Essentially, missing AYB info does not break any metric – it just means that portion of qualitative context is absent
	•	Private Sector & Chambers of Commerce (Federation of Yemeni Chambers of Commerce & Industry, and other business associations):
	•	URL: No centralized data site. Information comes via surveys or reports by the Chambers, business unions, or studies by organizations like Rethinking Yemen’s Economy or World Bank that include private sector data
	•	Access Method: Manual ingestion of any survey results or reports (e.g., a Chamber of Commerce survey on business climate, or customs authority data if shared through chambers)
	•	Authentication: None (would be public or semi-public info)
	•	Update Cadence: Irregular. Possibly occasional surveys (e.g., an annual business confidence survey if done, or one-off war impact assessments)
	•	Data Fields Available: Could include number of businesses operating, import/export volumes (if customs data shared), commodity prices from market surveys, business confidence indices, major constraints cited by businesses, etc. Often qualitative or aggregated statistics presented in reports
	•	Regime Split Handling: Not explicitly in data. If a survey is done, it might cover select governorates but not frame by regime. However, business conditions vary by area (the data, if any, would note region or city rather than political control explicitly)
	•	Licensing/Terms: Dependent on source; assume open use if published by chambers (with attribution)
	•	Reliability Score: C (data limited and not independently verified usually; but provides local insight when available)
	•	Coverage Type: Private sector economic data and anecdotes – covering trade, SME activity, etc. No consistent time series; mostly sporadic snapshots. YETO will incorporate 2010–present references as available
	•	Known Caveats: Much of this info is anecdotal or from small samples. For example, a chamber might report “60% of factories have closed since 2015” in a press statement – valuable, but not a regularly updated stat. Use in context only. Also there’s potential bias (chambers lobbying for certain policies might emphasize certain data)
	•	Mapped Sectors & Pages: Sectors – Private Sector Data (بيانات القطاع الخاص); Pages – Private Sector Dashboard (with any available stats, e.g., number of companies, trade volumes), Scenario Simulator (to tweak assumptions about private sector recovery)
	•	Ingestion Method: As part of YETO’s dynamic discovery, any study or data point regarding Yemen’s private sector is captured. For example, if a World Bank or Chamber study reports survey results, those results are manually input into YETO’s knowledge base (either as data points with source, or at least as a referenced document). The platform doesn’t anticipate regular feeds here; it’s more about curating whatever can be found. Key indicators (like “% of businesses operational”) might be stored as single-time observations tied to a year and source
	•	Fallbacks: Given there’s no expected routine data, there’s no automated gap alert for chambers data. However, if the platform design calls for a module on Private Sector and it remains empty, it will be evident in the Coverage Scorecard. The gap engine would then mark that as a sector with missing data coverage, prompting an action to find sources or input proxy indicators (e.g., using night lights as a proxy for private economic activity). Essentially, YETO handles this by flagging sector coverage gaps and using the Discovery Engine to continuously look out for any new private sector reports

Analytical, Proxy & Compliance Sources
	•	Remote Sensing – Night Lights (VIIRS/DMSP) (NASA/NOAA Satellite Data):
	•	URL: NOAA Earth Observation data archive (e.g. monthly VIIRS night-time lights composites accessible via AWS or NOAA Open Data)
	•	Access Method: Bulk download of raster images (.TIFF) and subsequent processing. No direct API for pre-aggregated Yemen data – YETO will process raw data
	•	Authentication: None (data is open, hosted on public servers)
	•	Update Cadence: Monthly composites (VIIRS Nighttime Lights produced monthly). DMSP-OLS data (older satellite) was annual until 2013, then VIIRS from 2012 onward monthly
	•	Data Fields Available: Nighttime light intensity per pixel (radiance values). YETO will derive summary metrics: e.g. total light output per governorate, average radiance for Yemen, etc., per month
	•	Regime Split Handling: Not directly applicable; however, YETO could aggregate lights by areas controlled if it overlays a political map. Primarily it’s subnational (grid) data that can be aggregated to any region
	•	Licensing/Terms: Open (U.S. government data)
	•	Reliability Score: C (as an economic proxy, it’s an indirect measure; technically data is reliable, but interpretation as economic activity needs care)
	•	Coverage Type: Proxy indicator of economic activity/electricity across Yemen. Monthly from 2012–present (VIIRS). Also includes historical (DMSP 2010–2013) for baseline comparison
	•	Known Caveats: Night lights can be affected by flares (gas flaring), seasonal factors (moonlight, clouds – though composites try to account for this), and conflict (blackouts). Also, two satellites have different calibration – a big jump from DMSP to VIIRS data. YETO must normalize or at least warn users when showing trends that span the change in sensors
	•	Mapped Sectors & Pages: Sectors – Proxy Indicators (المؤشرات البديلة); Pages – Macro Trends (as an alternative GDP proxy chart), Energy & Infrastructure (to infer electrification), Maps & Atlas, Timeline (to show lights change over war timeline)
	•	Ingestion Method: A specialized ETL process runs monthly (with a slight delay to allow NOAA to publish data). It downloads the Yemen-area subset of VIIRS nighttime lights raster. Then it computes aggregate values: e.g., sum of radiance in each governorate polygon, and national average radiance. These values are stored as monthly time series. The raw rasters are stored on S3 for archival or further analysis. (If needed, earlier DMSP annual data is also processed similarly for 2010–2013)
	•	Fallbacks: If the NOAA data server is unreachable or a particular month’s file is missing, the pipeline will try again next cycle. If a monthly file remains unavailable (sometimes data gets reprocessed or delayed), YETO logs it and skips that month (possibly interpolating or carrying last value forward with a flag). An ingestion alert is sent after a couple of failed attempts. A Data Gap Ticket will be made if two consecutive months of satellite data are missed, prompting an investigation (sometimes algorithm changes require using a different source). In case of a long-term blockage, alternative sources like Earth Observation portals or a third-party processed dataset (e.g., on World Bank’s API) could serve as fallbacks
	•	ACAPS Yemen Analysis (YETI) (ACAPS):
	•	URL: ACAPS Yemen Economic Tracking Initiative (YETI) reports on ACAPS website; typically PDF reports and data briefs
	•	Access Method: Manual download of reports (no API; ACAPS YETI is an analysis project that publishes periodic outputs)
	•	Authentication: None
	•	Update Cadence: Regular analytic outputs, roughly monthly or quarterly (for example, ACAPS releases scenario outlooks or bulletins periodically)
	•	Data Fields Available: Primarily narrative analysis of economic and humanitarian developments, forward-looking scenarios, risk alerts. May contain some data points or indices compiled by ACAPS (like an index of economic distress, or qualitative risk ratings)
	•	Regime Split Handling: Not applicable (analysis covers entire Yemen context, though it might discuss regional differences qualitatively)
	•	Licensing/Terms: Public domain for reports (ACAPS encourages dissemination, just cite them)
	•	Reliability Score: B+ (expert analysis, insightful but not official data; provides context and interpretation)
	•	Coverage Type: Analytical narrative covering recent economic trends, market functionality, humanitarian access, etc., with scenario predictions. 2018–present (ACAPS YETI active years)
	•	Known Caveats: No hard data series, mostly qualitative. The value is in narrative and expert opinion which can’t be “ingested” into a database like numeric data. However, it’s important for YETO’s AI to have this as contextual evidence for higher-level questions
	•	Mapped Sectors & Pages: Sectors – Research/Think-Tank (الأبحاث / مراكز الفكر); Pages – Scenario Simulator (ACAPS scenarios feed into assumptions), Research Hub (list of ACAPS reports), AI Assistant (for nuanced answers that require context beyond raw data)
	•	Ingestion Method: Each ACAPS YETI report is treated as a document in YETO’s Evidence Library. The PDF is downloaded, text-extracted, and indexed. Key scenario statements or any data mentioned (e.g. “Yemen’s food prices are 140% higher than pre-war”) are tagged and could be pulled into a knowledge graph. The platform may also have a curated summary of ACAPS scenarios available for the Scenario Simulator module. This ingestion is largely about capturing text for search and reference.
	•	Fallbacks: If ACAPS stops publishing YETI reports or the schedule is irregular, the system doesn’t flag it as a “data gap” in the same way (since this is supplementary analysis). However, the Discovery Engine will continue to look for any ACAPS Yemen publications. No direct alternative is needed; YETO will simply have less narrative context if not updated. If ACAPS changes its website structure (causing failed downloads), the ingestion will alert an admin to update the scraper. All in all, missing ACAPS updates is not a critical data gap but would be noted in content currency
	•	Rethinking Yemen’s Economy (RYE) (Sana’a Center Economic think-tank project):
	•	URL: Sana’a Center for Strategic Studies website, RYE project section (PDF policy briefs and papers)
	•	Access Method: Manual download of published papers (no API)
	•	Authentication: None
	•	Update Cadence: Occasional – the project ran from ~2017–2020 with a series of papers; new content beyond that depends on project continuation. (Likely a finite set of ~20 papers)
	•	Data Fields Available: Qualitative and some quantitative analysis on specific topics (e.g. fuel subsidy reforms, central bank split, private sector). They may include data tables or charts (e.g. timelines of fuel imports, or comparisons of monetary indicators) drawn from other sources
	•	Regime Split Handling: Not applicable (analysis often covers both sides, especially in context of central bank split or economic policies, but presented as unified discussion)
	•	Licensing/Terms: Public (think tank reports – free to use with attribution)
	•	Reliability Score: B+ (high-quality research, though not official data – provides insight and often uncovers hidden info via interviews)
	•	Coverage Type: Deep-dive reports on economic issues (fuel, banking, currency, etc.) spanning the war period. Not continuous data; case studies and policy analysis. YETO covers all published RYE content 2017–present
	•	Known Caveats: Each report is standalone – not a source of regularly updated indicators. Data within might come from elsewhere (which YETO may already have). The key value is in explanations and context that numbers alone don’t provide
	•	Mapped Sectors & Pages: Sectors – Research/Think-Tank (الأبحاث / مراكز الفكر); Pages – Stakeholder Perspectives (insights gleaned from RYE, e.g. sections in stakeholder profiles of central bank), Glossary/Methodology (detailed explanations of terms like Letter of Credit mechanism, drawn from RYE), Research Hub
	•	Ingestion Method: All RYE papers are added to the Research Library. The text is indexed so that the AI Assistant can pull knowledge from them. If any unique data tables are present, those figures are input into the system (with source citation). For example, if a RYE report provided a timeline of forex reserve drop, YETO would capture that data series if not available elsewhere, marked as coming from RYE. Mostly, ingestion is about referencing these reports for qualitative answers
	•	Fallbacks: Since RYE papers are a closed set (if the project has ended), there’s no ongoing update expected – thus no gap to fill. If new papers do appear, the discovery process will catch them. If the Sana’a Center site is down or a PDF link broken, YETO operators will manually retrieve via alternate means (like contacting the Center). No automated fallback beyond our continuous scanning for new research publications
	•	UN & National Sanctions Lists (UN, OFAC, EU, UK) (United Nations, US OFAC, EU Council, UK HMT sanctions):
	•	URL: UN Security Council consolidated sanctions list (XML file updated regularly); US OFAC Specially Designated Nationals (SDN) list CSV; EU and UK sanctions list CSVs. (These include entries related to Yemen, among others)
	•	Access Method: Automated download of the latest lists from each authority. The UN provides an XML of all sanctions; OFAC provides a CSV; EU/UK provide downloadable lists (often PDF or Excel converted to CSV)
	•	Authentication: None (public resources)
	•	Update Cadence: As needed – updates occur whenever sanctions are added/removed, which can be multiple times per year (no fixed schedule, but checked daily or weekly for changes)
	•	Data Fields Available: For each sanctioned entity/person: Name, aliases, date of listing, sanction program/regime (e.g. UNSCR 2140 Yemen), identifying information (DOB, passport for individuals; location, registration for entities), reason for listing, dates of updates, etc.
	•	Regime Split Handling: Not applicable (global list; entries might be associated with different Yemeni parties but that’s not structured by regime, except implicitly by sanction program)
	•	Licensing/Terms: Public domain (official government/UN legal notices)
	•	Reliability Score: A (official lists; purely factual)
	•	Coverage Type: All individuals and entities sanctioned in relation to Yemen (and in general). YETO will maintain a subset relevant to Yemen (e.g. those listed under Yemen-related programs, plus Yemeni nationals listed under global programs). Time coverage 2010–present (UN Yemen sanctions regime started in 2014; OFAC and others had earlier terror listings)
	•	Known Caveats: Names can have multiple spellings (Arabic transliteration issues). Matching across lists requires careful normalization. Also, sanctions status can change (delistings, new aliases) – historical tracking is needed to show if someone was once sanctioned. YETO must regularly update to reflect current status
	•	Mapped Sectors & Pages: Sectors – Sanctions & Compliance (العقوبات والامتثال); Pages – Sanctions Dashboard (list of sanctioned entities with filters), Stakeholder Profiles (flag if a person/org is sanctioned), AI Compliance Q&A (assistant can answer sanctions-related queries), Timeline (sanctions events)
	•	Ingestion Method: A daily job checks each source: downloads the UN XML, the latest OFAC SDN CSV, EU and UK lists. The ingestion script parses these and filters entries with a Yemen nexus (e.g. UN’s list code for Yemen, or OFAC program “YEMEN” or known Yemeni nationals in Al-Qaida list, etc.). All entries (Yemen-related and others) can be stored in a compliance database, but YETO highlights the Yemen-related ones on the platform. Each entry’s data (names, IDs) is stored for search and cross-matching (for example, to flag if a company in YETO’s stakeholder database appears on a sanctions list). The provenance ledger logs the source and date for each record
	•	Fallbacks: If any list fails to download (say the UN site is down), that day’s job will skip that source and report a warning. The system continues with others, and will try the UN list the next day. If a format changes (XML schema update or CSV columns change), the parser error is logged and an alert sent to update the ingestion code. Persistent failures (e.g., no update from a source that should have updates or continuous download errors) trigger a Gap Ticket for investigation. In practice, since these are official resources, downtime is rare; however, YETO ensures partial updates (if one source is down, others still update) and logs any anomalies. All sanction data changes are versioned, so if a fallback is needed (like using a cached previous list), the platform can temporarily use last known data and mark it as potentially outdated until the feed resumes

2. Ingestion Pipeline Logic

Data Flow from Sources to Storage

All data flows through a structured ETL pipeline that channels source inputs into YETO’s databases and indexes while preserving provenance. For numeric and structured data, the pipeline fetches raw data (via API responses, CSV files, etc.) and first lands it in a raw storage (S3 or a staging schema in PostgreSQL). Each ingestion run records metadata (source ID, fetch timestamp, raw file hash) in a Provenance Ledger. The data is then transformed and loaded into YETO’s PostgreSQL database, organized by thematic tables (e.g. economic_indicators, trade_stats, projects, conflict_events). Simultaneously, a provenance record is attached at the granular level – every data point or record gets an associated reference in the ledger (source name, original dataset, publication date, licensing). After loading structured data, the pipeline updates derived aggregates or materialized views (for faster dashboard queries) as needed.

For documents and unstructured content (reports, PDFs, text), the pipeline stores the original files in an S3 bucket (or similar blob store) and extracts text to index in the vectorized document store. This vector store (backed by pgvector in PostgreSQL and/or OpenSearch for text search) holds embeddings of documents and paragraphs, enabling semantic search for the AI assistant. The raw text is also stored or cached for full-text querying (OpenSearch index if deployed). The pipeline links each document or text chunk to its provenance: e.g. a UN report’s metadata (title, source, date) is recorded so that any quote or data pulled from it can be cited.

Throughout the flow, data integrity is enforced: the transformation layer ensures incoming fields match expected schema (e.g., numeric types, valid category codes). If any anomalies are detected (missing required fields, out-of-range values), the pipeline can reject or flag those records for review. Accepted data then goes into the production database, and a snapshot of the raw input (or a checksum hash) is retained to allow later verification against source.

Orchestration & Scheduling

AWS EventBridge is used to schedule and trigger ingestion jobs according to the cadence defined in the Master Source Registry. Each source (or group of sources) has a rule – e.g., a daily cron trigger for daily sources (midnight UTC to fetch yesterday’s updates), weekly triggers (e.g. every Monday 01:00 UTC) for weekly sources, monthly triggers (1st of month for monthly/quarterly data), and so on. EventBridge events kick off AWS Step Functions workflows that orchestrate the multi-step ETL for each source. For example, a Step Function for “WorldBankIndicators” runs through steps: (1) API calls for new data, (2) parse JSON and load to staging, (3) transform to normalized tables, (4) update provenance ledger, (5) run integrity checks, (6) success/failure notification.

Different sources can share Step Function templates if their process is similar (with parameters for URLs, parsing logic), enabling reuse of ETL patterns. Step Functions manage retries and branching logic (e.g., if an API returns no new data, skip load but still mark pipeline run complete). Parallelization is employed where possible: for instance, one step might fetch multiple pages of an API concurrently, or process multiple CSV files in parallel, and then a following step merges the results.

Orchestration example: Every day, EventBridge triggers a DailyUpdate Step Function. Within it, tasks for each daily source run (potentially in parallel where appropriate): ReliefWeb API fetch, FTS API fetch, sanctions list downloads, etc. Each task’s status is logged. On Mondays, a WeeklyUpdate workflow runs, handling sources like IATI and ACLED. On the first of the month, a MonthlyUpdate workflow triggers, fetching sources like World Bank, WFP, etc. There are also event-based triggers: e.g., when a new document is uploaded by an admin (manual ingestion), it can trigger a document processing function (for OCR and translation).

All these processes are coordinated in AWS and utilize cloud logging (CloudWatch) to record each run. If a job fails, Step Functions catches the error and marks the workflow as failed after optional retries, which then raises an alert (e.g., an SNS notification or internal dashboard update). The orchestration design ensures the system knows at any given time which jobs succeeded, failed, or are pending, forming the basis of an ingestion monitor for administrators.

Idempotency & Integrity

Each ingestion job is designed to be idempotent, meaning running it multiple times on the same input won’t duplicate data or corrupt results. This is achieved by using unique keys and checksums: for example, when loading time series data, the ETL uses a composite key (source + indicator + date) and either upserts (update/insert) or performs a deduplication check on insert. If the same record already exists (e.g., we fetched the same month twice), it will not create a duplicate entry. Similarly, document ingestion computes a hash of each document file; if an identical file was already ingested, it will be recognized and skipped or marked as a new version instead of a duplicate.

Retry safety: The pipelines implement retries with exponential backoff for transient failures (network issues, API timeouts). If a job fails mid-way (say, halfway through parsing a large dataset), the system can safely resume or restart without partial duplicates. For instance, partial data written to a staging table is either erased on failure or written with a batch ID that gets overwritten on retry. A durable log of ingestion runs (in a table ingestion_runs) tracks which step completed. On retry, the pipeline can check this log and decide whether to continue from the last safe checkpoint or start over. For example, if a file was downloaded but parsing failed, the retry might skip re-downloading if the file exists and go straight to parsing, unless the file could be corrupt.

Integrity checks: After each load, the system performs validation checks:
	•	Schema conformity: Ensures the loaded data matches the expected schema (all required columns present, data types correct). If a schema drift is detected (e.g., a new column appears or a column disappears in source), the job flags an error for developers to address (since that might indicate the source format changed).
